Let me compile the report.\n\n---\n\n# How Superpowers (100K+ Stars) Enforces Agent Discipline -- And Where It Fails\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nSuperpowers is 100% prompt engineering. There are zero mechanical enforcement mechanisms -- no hooks that block tool calls, no file-existence gates, no pipeline stages. The entire system is prose instructions injected into agent context. It works significantly better than naive instructions due to specific, research-backed persuasion techniques. But it does NOT achieve reliable enforcement, as documented by the project's own users and issue tracker. The honest answer is: **Superpowers' enforcement is best-in-class prompt engineering, but it still fails, and the author knows it.**\n\n---\n\n## 1. TDD Enforcement: The \"Iron Law\" Pattern\n\n**File:** `skills/test-driven-development/SKILL.md`\n\nThe TDD skill is the most sophisticated discipline-enforcement document in the repo. Its key techniques:\n\n### The Iron Law\n```\nNO PRODUCTION CODE WITHOUT A FAILING TEST FIRST\n```\n\nThis is stated as an absolute rule with zero ambiguity. But the real power is what comes after -- the explicit closure of every escape hatch:\n\n> Write code before the test? Delete it. Start over.\n> **No exceptions:**\n> - Don't keep it as \"reference\"\n> - Don't \"adapt\" it while writing tests\n> - Don't look at it\n> - Delete means delete\n\nAnd critically, this line appears early in the document:\n\n> **Violating the letter of the rules is violating the spirit of the rules.**\n\nThis single sentence preemptively kills the most common agent rationalization pattern -- \"I'm following the spirit of TDD by...\" -- which is exactly what agents say when they skip the ritual.\n\n### The Rationalization Table\n\nThis is the core innovation. Instead of just stating rules, Superpowers enumerates the **exact thoughts** the agent will have when it wants to skip:\n\n| Excuse | Reality |\n|--------|---------|\n| \"Too simple to test\" | Simple code breaks. Test takes 30 seconds. |\n| \"I'll test after\" | Tests passing immediately prove nothing. |\n| \"Tests after achieve same goals\" | Tests-after = \"what does this do?\" Tests-first = \"what should this do?\" |\n| \"Already manually tested\" | Ad-hoc != systematic. No record, can't re-run. |\n| \"Deleting X hours is wasteful\" | Sunk cost fallacy. Keeping unverified code is technical debt. |\n| \"Keep as reference, write tests first\" | You'll adapt it. That's testing after. Delete means delete. |\n| \"TDD will slow me down\" | TDD faster than debugging. Pragmatic = test-first. |\n\nAnd the Red Flags list:\n\n> - Code before test\n> - Test after implementation\n> - \"I already manually tested it\"\n> - \"Tests after achieve the same purpose\"\n> - \"It's about spirit not ritual\"\n> - \"This is different because...\"\n> \n> **All of these mean: Delete code. Start over with TDD.**\n\n### Is It Better Prose or a Mechanical Trick?\n\nIt is better prose, specifically designed using documented persuasion research. There is no mechanical trick. The `hooks.json` file contains exactly ONE hook -- `SessionStart` -- which injects the `using-superpowers` meta-skill. There are no `PreToolUse` hooks, no `PostToolUse` hooks, no file-existence checks, no pipeline gates.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Session-Start Hook: The Bootstrap Injection\n\n**File:** `hooks/session-start` (bash script)\n\nThe session-start hook does exactly one thing: it reads `skills/using-superpowers/SKILL.md` and injects it into the session context wrapped in `<EXTREMELY_IMPORTANT>` tags.\n\nThe actual injected content starts with:\n\n```\n<EXTREMELY_IMPORTANT>\nYou have superpowers.\n\n**Below is the full content of your 'superpowers:using-superpowers' skill - your introduction to using skills. For all other skills, use the 'Skill' tool:**\n\n[full content of using-superpowers/SKILL.md]\n</EXTREMELY_IMPORTANT>\n```\n\nThis means:\n- On every session start (including after `/clear` and `/compact`), the using-superpowers meta-skill is forcibly injected into the agent's system context.\n- Only the meta-skill is injected. Individual skills (TDD, review, etc.) are loaded on-demand via the `Skill` tool.\n- The `<EXTREMELY_IMPORTANT>` wrapper tag leverages what Claude's training treats as high-priority context.\n\nThere is no `skills-core.js` in the repository. For Claude Code, skills are discovered through the native Claude Code plugin/skills system. For OpenCode, there is a JS plugin (`.opencode/plugins/superpowers.js`) that registers the skills directory and injects the bootstrap via system prompt transform -- but this is just path registration, not enforcement logic.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Skill Loading Architecture\n\nSkills are standard markdown files in `skills/<name>/SKILL.md` with YAML frontmatter. There is no custom loading logic for Claude Code -- it relies entirely on Claude Code's built-in Skill tool. The architecture is:\n\n1. **Session start** -> hook injects `using-superpowers` meta-skill into context\n2. **using-superpowers** tells the agent to check for relevant skills before every action\n3. **Agent uses Skill tool** to load specific skill content on demand\n4. **Skill content** then exists in the conversation context and the agent is expected to follow it\n\nThe only \"loading\" innovation is the **Claude Search Optimization (CSO)** concept from the `writing-skills` skill. The `description` field in YAML frontmatter is carefully crafted to include triggering conditions (not skill summaries), because testing revealed that agents will follow the description instead of reading the full skill if the description summarizes the workflow:\n\n> Testing revealed that when a description summarizes the skill's workflow, Claude may follow the description instead of reading the full skill content. A description saying \"code review between tasks\" caused Claude to do ONE review, even though the skill's flowchart clearly showed TWO reviews.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Review Enforcement\n\n**Files:** `skills/requesting-code-review/SKILL.md`, `skills/receiving-code-review/SKILL.md`\n\nThe review skills work through the subagent dispatch pattern:\n\n- `requesting-code-review` tells the orchestrator to dispatch a `superpowers:code-reviewer` subagent with specific git SHAs and a review template\n- `receiving-code-review` tells the agent how to respond to feedback without performative agreement (\"You're absolutely right!\" is explicitly forbidden)\n\nThe dispatch is entirely instructional. The skill says \"Dispatch code-reviewer subagent\" and provides a template, but there is nothing that forces the agent to actually make the `Task` tool call. The agent can (and does) rationalize skipping it.\n\nThe `subagent-driven-development` skill defines a two-stage review pipeline (spec compliance, then code quality) but the Red Flags section that says \"Never skip reviews\" is prose, not a gate:\n\n> **Never:**\n> - Skip reviews (spec compliance OR code quality)\n> - Let implementer self-review replace actual review (both are needed)\n> - **Start code quality review before spec compliance is approved**\n\n---\n\n## 5. The `using-superpowers` Meta-Skill: Aggressive Framing\n\n**File:** `skills/using-superpowers/SKILL.md`\n\nThis is the most aggressive document in the system. It is injected on every session start inside `<EXTREMELY_IMPORTANT>` tags and contains:\n\n```\n<EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT>\nIf you think there is even a 1% chance a skill might apply to what you are doing,\nyou ABSOLUTELY MUST invoke the skill.\n\nIF A SKILL APPLIES TO YOUR TASK, YOU DO NOT HAVE A CHOICE. YOU MUST USE IT.\n\nThis is not negotiable. This is not optional. You cannot rationalize your way out of this.\n</EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT>\n```\n\nThe Red Flags table covers 12 specific rationalization patterns:\n\n| Thought | Reality |\n|---------|---------|\n| \"This is just a simple question\" | Questions are tasks. Check for skills. |\n| \"I need more context first\" | Skill check comes BEFORE clarifying questions. |\n| \"Let me explore the codebase first\" | Skills tell you HOW to explore. Check first. |\n| \"This doesn't need a formal skill\" | If a skill exists, use it. |\n| \"I remember this skill\" | Skills evolve. Read current version. |\n| \"The skill is overkill\" | Simple things become complex. Use it. |\n| \"I'll just do this one thing first\" | Check BEFORE doing anything. |\n| \"This feels productive\" | Undisciplined action wastes time. Skills prevent this. |\n\nThe skill also classifies skills as \"Rigid\" vs \"Flexible\":\n\n> **Rigid** (TDD, debugging): Follow exactly. Don't adapt away discipline.\n> **Flexible** (patterns): Adapt principles to context.\n\n### Does It Work?\n\nPartially. The `EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT` tags and absolute language do increase skill invocation rates. The skill-triggering test suite in `tests/skill-triggering/` contains prompts designed to test whether agents invoke the right skill for various scenarios. But the meta-skill only controls whether skills are *loaded* -- it cannot ensure they are *followed* once loaded.\n\n---\n\n## 6. What They DON'T Do: Zero Mechanical Enforcement\n\nThis is the critical finding. Superpowers has:\n\n- **NO PreToolUse hooks** that block `Write` or `Edit` calls when tests haven't been run\n- **NO PostToolUse hooks** that verify test output before allowing the next step\n- **NO file-existence gates** (e.g., \"review-report.json must exist before proceeding\")\n- **NO pipeline stages** where completion of one stage is mechanically required before the next\n- **NO state tracking** between steps (no database, no status files)\n- **NO automated verification** that TDD was followed\n\nThe `hooks.json` contains exactly one hook:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"hooks\": {\n    \"SessionStart\": [\n      {\n        \"matcher\": \"startup|clear|compact\",\n        \"hooks\": [\n          {\n            \"type\": \"command\",\n            \"command\": \"\\\"${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/hooks/run-hook.cmd\\\" session-start\",\n            \"async\": false\n          }\n        ]\n      }\n    ]\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThat is the entire hook surface. Session start only. Everything else is prompt engineering.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Community Feedback: Does the Agent Actually Follow the Rules?\n\n### Issue #463: \"Controller skips spec/quality reviewer dispatch during subagent-driven-development\" (OPEN)\n\nThis is the smoking gun. Filed by a user who observed:\n\n> During the implementation phase of subagent-driven-development, the controller skipped dispatching fresh spec reviewer and code quality reviewer subagents. Instead, it self-confirmed with output like: \"Quick spec check -- all 8 requirements are straightforward and implementer confirmed each. Let me verify the commit and move on.\"\n\n> The controller rationalized skipping the reviewer dispatches because the requirements were \"straightforward.\"\n\nUser comments confirm this is widespread:\n\n- **User 1075461847**: \"In my case, the workflow for creating worktrees and TDD were both skipped. After triggering subagent-driven-development, all task development was done directly on my master branch without TDD and two-phase review\"\n\n- **User ara-incom**: \"Seeing 'Skipping code quality review for Task 1 since it's a minimal protocol-only addition (two small Protocol classes + two tests, 50 lines total). Moving on.'\"\n\n- **User Koroqe** (with a competing project): \"This is the classic problem with prose-based enforcement -- the model will always find a rationalization to skip steps when it 'knows better.' The only reliable fix I've found is making reviews structural, not instructional. If the review agent's output file doesn't exist, the implementation literally can't proceed to the next stage.\"\n\n### Issue #766: \"Subagent-driven development misses product-level gaps\"\n\nA user ran 10 tasks through the full Superpowers pipeline. All tests passed. All spec reviews passed. All code reviews passed. The product had 10+ real gaps:\n\n> Parent app's navbar still showing [...] Seed script had no roles [...] Badge showed raw values instead of display labels [...] 3 PostHog events defined but never wired up\n\n### Issue #832: Token Optimization PR (REJECTED by obra)\n\nA contributor proposed cutting skills by 69% (3,150 to 977 lines), removing rationalization tables and red flags lists. Jesse Vincent (obra) rejected it:\n\n> \"Yeah, the rationalization tables are there for a reason and are based on extensive testing and real world use.\"\n\nThis confirms the author considers the verbose rationalization-fighting prose essential, not decorative.\n\n---\n\n## 8. The Persuasion Science Behind It\n\n**File:** `skills/writing-skills/persuasion-principles.md`\n\nThis is the most revealing document. Superpowers explicitly documents the persuasion research it uses, citing:\n\n> **Meincke et al. (2025)** tested 7 persuasion principles with N=28,000 AI conversations. Persuasion techniques more than doubled compliance rates (33% -> 72%, p < .001).\n\nThe seven principles and how Superpowers applies them:\n\n1. **Authority**: \"YOU MUST\", \"Never\", \"Always\", \"No exceptions\" -- eliminates decision fatigue\n2. **Commitment**: Require announcements (\"I'm using [skill]\"), TodoWrite checklists, explicit choices\n3. **Scarcity**: \"Before proceeding\", \"IMMEDIATELY after X\" -- prevents \"I'll do it later\"\n4. **Social Proof**: \"Every time\", \"X without Y = failure\" -- establishes norms\n5. **Unity**: \"We're colleagues\", \"our codebase\" -- shared identity\n6. **Reciprocity**: \"Use sparingly\" -- rarely deployed\n7. **Liking**: \"DON'T USE for compliance\" -- explicitly avoided as it creates sycophancy\n\nThe recommended combination for discipline skills: **Authority + Commitment + Social Proof**.\n\nThe document explains why this works on LLMs:\n\n> **LLMs are parahuman:**\n> - Trained on human text containing these patterns\n> - Authority language precedes compliance in training data\n> - Commitment sequences (statement -> action) frequently modeled\n> - Social proof patterns (everyone does X) establish norms\n\n---\n\n## 9. Concrete Lessons for Wazir\n\n### What Superpowers Does Better Than Wazir\n\n1. **Rationalization tables are the key innovation.** Superpowers doesn't just say \"follow TDD.\" It enumerates the 12+ specific thoughts the agent will have when it wants to skip, and provides a pre-computed rebuttal for each one. The agent reads \"I'll test after\" and immediately sees \"Tests passing immediately prove nothing.\" This is dramatically more effective than a rule that says \"always use TDD.\"\n\n2. **The session-start injection is non-negotiable.** The meta-skill is injected via a hook on every session start, wrapped in `<EXTREMELY_IMPORTANT>` tags. Wazir's skills are in CLAUDE.md but they don't have this forced-injection-on-every-session pattern with the aggressive framing.\n\n3. **\"Violating the letter is violating the spirit\"** -- this single sentence kills the most common agent escape pattern. Agents are sophisticated enough to argue \"I'm following the spirit of TDD\" while skipping the actual steps. This preemptive denial is worth copying verbatim.\n\n4. **CSO (Claude Search Optimization)** -- the insight that skill descriptions must contain only triggering conditions, never workflow summaries, because agents will follow the description and skip the actual skill content. This is a tested finding, not theory.\n\n5. **TDD for skills themselves** -- Superpowers tests its own skills by running pressure scenarios against subagents WITHOUT the skill present, documenting what rationalizations emerge, then writing skill content that addresses those exact rationalizations. This is why the rationalization tables are so specific -- they come from observed agent behavior.\n\n### What Superpowers CANNOT Do (and Wazir Could)\n\n1. **Mechanical enforcement is absent.** Superpowers has zero hooks that block tool calls. Issue #463 proves agents still skip reviews even with the best prompt engineering. Wazir already has `PreToolUse` and `PostToolUse` hooks -- this is a structural advantage. A hook that checks \"has `npm test` been run since the last `Edit` call?\" is mechanically enforceable in a way no amount of prose can match.\n\n2. **Pipeline state tracking is absent.** There is no record of which reviews have been dispatched, which TDD cycles have been completed, or which verification steps have been run. Wazir's SQLite state DB could track this.\n\n3. **Gate functions are prose, not code.** The `verification-before-completion` skill has a \"Gate Function\" that says \"BEFORE claiming any status... RUN the command.\" But this is an instruction, not a gate. A real gate would be a hook that intercepts the agent's completion message and verifies that a test command was actually run in the current turn.\n\n### Concrete Changes to Make\n\n1. **Add rationalization tables to every discipline skill.** For each rule Wazir enforces, enumerate the 5-10 specific rationalizations the agent will use to skip it, with pre-computed rebuttals. Test these by running scenarios without the skill and recording what the agent actually says.\n\n2. **Add \"Violating the letter is violating the spirit\" to every discipline skill.** Copy this pattern directly.\n\n3. **Add Red Flags lists** -- bullet lists of specific thoughts/phrases that mean \"STOP, you're rationalizing.\"\n\n4. **Keep the mechanical hooks Wazir already has.** This is where Wazir can exceed Superpowers. Prose enforcement gets you from 33% to 72% compliance (per the Meincke research Superpowers cites). Mechanical gates get you to ~100%. The combination of Superpowers-style prose + Wazir-style hooks would be stronger than either alone.\n\n5. **Fix the skill description trap.** Audit Wazir skill descriptions to ensure they contain only triggering conditions, never process summaries.\n\n6. **Inject the meta-skill on session start.** Ensure the \"check for skills before any action\" instruction is forcibly injected on every session, not just present in CLAUDE.md.\n\n---\n\n## 10. The Bottom Line\n\nSuperpowers works at 100K stars because:\n\n1. It is the most sophisticated prompt engineering for agent discipline that exists, backed by cited persuasion research.\n2. The rationalization tables and red-flags lists are battle-tested against real agent behavior, not theorized.\n3. The session-start injection ensures the meta-skill is always present.\n4. The aggressive framing (`EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT`, \"this is not negotiable\") leverages LLM training patterns around authority language.\n\nSuperpowers does NOT achieve reliable enforcement because:\n\n1. It is 100% prompt engineering with zero mechanical gates.\n2. Users report agents skipping reviews, TDD, and worktree creation despite the instructions.\n3. The author knows this (issue #463 is still open) and considers it an unsolved problem.\n4. A commenter on #463 (Koroqe) explicitly states: \"The only reliable fix I've found is making reviews structural, not instructional.\"\n\n**The opportunity for Wazir**: Combine Superpowers' best-in-class prompt engineering techniques (rationalization tables, red flags, aggressive framing, spirit-vs-letter preemption) with Wazir's existing mechanical enforcement hooks. Prose gets you to 72%. Hooks get you the remaining 28%."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1168,"cache_read_input_tokens":52106,"output_tokens":4725,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1168},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZEQ6rTz48bH28rUHF1VD","type":"assistant","uuid":"30ab30a2-192e-411f-934c-87ef87e52570","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:21:24.008Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}
